A reason link is weaker than a trigger, it only suggests that some service may be or might have been a reason for some action, but not that this reason requires/required the action to be taken. Also, as opposed to the trigger, there is no strong timely relation between the reason and the action. As well as providing various types of information about the rationale for a service, the RSON act relationship is routinely used between a SBADM act and an OBS act to describe the indication for use of a medication. Child concepts may be used to describe types of indication.</p>\n<p><em>Discussion:</em> In prior releases, the code &quot;SUGG&quot; (suggests) was expressed as &quot;an inversion of the reason link.&quot; That code has been retired in favor of the inversion indicator that is an attribute of ActRelationship.</p>\n</div></td><td>10321</td><td>active</td><td>true</td><td>true</td><td>reasonOf</td><td>reason</td><td>CA_______</td><td>CA_______</td><td>action</td><td>reason</td><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>_ActRelationshipConditional</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">      BLOCK<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-BLOCK\"> </a></td><td>blocks</td><td><div><p><strong>Definition:</strong> The source act is performed to block the effects of the target act. The priorityNumber attribute is used to weigh refinements as preferred over other alternative refinements.</p>\n<p>Example: several routing options for a drug are specified as one SubstanceAdministration for the general treatment with attached refinements for the various routing options.</p>\n</div></td><td>10347</td><td>active</td><td>false</td><td>true</td><td>optionFor</td><td>option</td><td>BN_______</td><td>BN_______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SEQL</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">    RCHAL<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-RCHAL\"> </a></td><td>re-challenge</td><td><div><p>**Description:**A relationship in which the target act is carried out to determine whether an effect attributed to the source act can be recreated.</p>\n</div></td><td>22044</td><td>active</td><td>false</td><td>true</td><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SEQL</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">    REV<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-REV\"> </a></td><td>reverses</td><td><div><p>A relationship between a source Act that seeks to reverse or undo the action of the prior target Act.</p>\n<p>Example: A posted financial transaction (e.g., a debit transaction) was applied in error and must be reversed (e.g., by a credit transaction) the credit transaction is identified as an undo (or reversal) of the prior target transaction.</p>\n<p>Constraints: the &quot;completion track&quot; mood of the target Act must be equally or more &quot;actual&quot; than the source act. I.e., when the target act is EVN the source act can be EVN, or any INT. If the target act is INT, the source act can be INT.</p>\n</div></td><td>14898</td><td>active</td><td>false</td><td>true</td><td>reversal</td><td>reversalOf</td><td>BK_______</td><td>BK_______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SEQL</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">    RPLC<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-RPLC\"> </a></td><td>replaces</td><td><div><p>A replacement source act replaces an existing target act. The state of the target act being replaced becomes obselete, but the act is typically still retained in the system for historical reference. The source and target must be of the same type.</p>\n</div></td><td>10338</td><td>active</td><td>false</td><td>true</td><td>replacement</td><td>replacementOf</td><td>BI_______</td><td>BI_______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SEQL</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">    SUCC<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-SUCC\"> </a></td><td>succeeds</td><td><div><p><strong>Definition:</strong> A new act that carries forward the intention of the original act, but does not completely replace it. The status of the predecessor act must be 'completed'. The original act is the target act and the successor is the source act.</p>\n</div></td><td>11616</td><td>active</td><td>false</td><td>true</td><td>successor</td><td>predecessor</td><td>BIA______</td><td>BIA______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SEQL</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">    UPDT<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-UPDT\"> </a></td><td>updates (condition)</td><td><div><p>A condition thread relationship specifically links condition nodes together to form a condition thread. The source is the new condition node and the target links to the most recent node of the existing condition thread.</p>\n</div></td><td>10340</td><td>active</td><td>false</td><td>true</td><td>update</td><td>updateOf</td><td>BE_______</td><td>BE_______</td><td>new head of thread</td><td>old head of thread</td><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SEQL</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">    XCRPT<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-XCRPT\"> </a></td><td>Excerpts</td><td><div><p>The source is an excerpt from the target.</p>\n</div></td><td>18660</td><td>active</td><td>false</td><td>true</td><td>excerpt</td><td>excerptFrom</td><td>BM_______</td><td>BM_______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SEQL</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">      VRXCRPT<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-VRXCRPT\"> </a></td><td>Excerpt verbatim</td><td><div><p>The source is a direct quote from the target.</p>\n</div></td><td>18661</td><td>active</td><td>false</td><td>true</td><td>verbatimExcerpt</td><td>verbatimExcerptFrom</td><td>BMA______</td><td>BMA______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>XCRPT</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">    XFRM<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-XFRM\"> </a></td><td>transformation</td><td><div><p>Used when the target Act is a transformation of the source Act. (For instance, used to show that a CDA document is a transformation of a DICOM SR document.)</p>\n</div></td><td>11624</td><td>active</td><td>false</td><td>true</td><td>transformation</td><td>transformationOf</td><td>BL_______</td><td>BL_______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SEQL</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">  SPRT<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-SPRT\"> </a></td><td>has support</td><td><div><p>Used to indicate that an existing service is suggesting evidence for a new observation. The assumption of support is attributed to the same actor who asserts the observation. Source must be an observation, target may be any service (e.g., to indicate a status post).</p>\n</div></td><td>10330</td><td>active</td><td/><td>true</td><td>supportOf</td><td>support</td><td>DA_______</td><td>DA_______</td><td/><td>supporting evidence</td><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>ART</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">    SPRTBND<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-SPRTBND\"> </a></td><td>has bounded support</td><td><div><p>A specialization of &quot;has support&quot; (SPRT), used to relate a secondary observation to a Region of Interest on a multidimensional observation, if the ROI specifies the true boundaries of the secondary observation as opposed to only marking the approximate area. For example, if the start and end of an ST elevation episode is visible in an EKG, this relation would indicate the ROI bounds the &quot;ST elevation&quot; observation -- the ROI defines the true beginning and ending of the episode. Conversely, if a ROI simply contains ST elevation, but it does not define the bounds (start and end) of the episode, the more general &quot;has support&quot; relation is used. Likewise, if a ROI on an image defines the true bounds of a &quot;1st degree burn&quot;, the relation &quot;has bounded support&quot; is used; but if the ROI only points to the approximate area of the burn, the general &quot;has support&quot; relation is used.</p>\n</div></td><td>17899</td><td>active</td><td/><td>true</td><td>boundedSupportOf</td><td>boundedSupport</td><td>DAA______</td><td>DAA______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SPRT</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">  SUBJ<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-SUBJ\"> </a></td><td>has subject</td><td><div><p>Relates an Act to its subject Act that the first Act is primarily concerned with.</p>\n<p>Examples</p>\n<ol>\n<li>The first Act may be a ControlAct manipulating the subject Act</li>\n<li>The first act is a region of interest (ROI) that defines a region within the subject Act.</li>\n<li>The first act is a reporting or notification Act, that echos the subject Act for a specific new purpose.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Constraints</p>\n<p>An Act may have multiple subject acts.</p>\n<p>Rationale</p>\n<p>The ActRelationshipType &quot;has subject&quot; is similar to the ParticipationType &quot;subject&quot;, Acts that primarily operate on physical subjects use the Participation, those Acts that primarily operate on other Acts (other information) use the ActRelationship.</p>\n</div></td><td>13971</td><td>active</td><td/><td>true</td><td>subjectOf</td><td>subject</td><td>DB_______</td><td>DB_______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>ART</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">    QUALF<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-QUALF\"> </a></td><td>has qualifier</td><td><div><p>The target observation qualifies (refines) the semantics of the source observation.</p>\n<p><em>UsageNote:</em> This is not intended to replace concept refinement and qualification via vocabulary. It is used when there are multiple components which together provide the complete understanding of the source Act.</p>\n</div></td><td>23598</td><td>active</td><td/><td>true</td><td>qualifies</td><td>hasQualifier</td><td>DBA______</td><td>DBA______</td><td>any Act</td><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>SUBJ</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">  SUMM<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-SUMM\"> </a></td><td>summarized by</td><td><div><p>An act that contains summary values for a list or set of subordinate acts. For example, a summary of transactions for a particular accounting period.</p>\n</div></td><td>15988</td><td>active</td><td/><td>true</td><td>summaryOf</td><td>summary</td><td>DM_______</td><td>DM_______</td><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>ART</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">  VALUE<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-VALUE\"> </a></td><td>has value</td><td><div><p>**Description:**Indicates that the target Act represents the result of the source observation Act.</p>\n<p><strong>FormalConstraint:</strong> Source Act must be an Observation or specialization there-of. Source Act must not have the value attribute specified</p>\n<p><strong>UsageNote:</strong> This relationship allows the result of an observation to be fully expressed as RIM acts as opposed to being embedded in the value attribute. For example, sending a Document act as the result of an imaging observation, sending a list of Procedures and/or other acts as the result of a medical history observation.</p>\n<p>The valueNegationInd attribute on the source Act has the same semantics of &quot;negated finding&quot; when it applies to the target of a VALUE ActRelationship as it does to the value attribute. On the other hand, if the ActRelationship.negationInd is true for a VALUE ActRelationship, that means the specified observation does not have the indicated value but does not imply a negated finding. Because the semantics are extremely close, it is recommended that Observation.valueNegationInd be used, not ActRelationship.negationInd.</p>\n<p><strong>OpenIssue:</strong> The implications of negationInd on ActRelationship and the valueNegationind on Observation.</p>\n</div></td><td>23319</td><td>active</td><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td>ART</td></tr><tr style=\"background-color: #ffeeee\"><td>1</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">CURE<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-CURE\"> </a></td><td>curative indication</td><td/><td>21642</td><td>retired</td><td/><td>true</td><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td/></tr><tr style=\"background-color: #ffeeee\"><td>1</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">CURE.ADJ<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-CURE.46ADJ\"> </a></td><td>adjunct curative indication</td><td/><td>21643</td><td>retired</td><td/><td>true</td><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td/></tr><tr style=\"background-color: #ffeeee\"><td>1</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">MTGT.ADJ<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-MTGT.46ADJ\"> </a></td><td>adjunct mitigation</td><td/><td>21641</td><td>retired</td><td/><td>true</td><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td/></tr><tr style=\"background-color: #ffeeee\"><td>1</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">RACT<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-RACT\"> </a></td><td/><td/><td>14892</td><td>retired</td><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td/></tr><tr style=\"background-color: #ffeeee\"><td>1</td><td style=\"white-space:nowrap\">SUGG<a name=\"v3-ActRelationshipType-SUGG\"> </a></td><td/><td/><td>10322</td><td>retired</td><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td/><td>&amp;</td><td>&amp;</td><td/><td/><td/><td/></tr></table></div>"

fhir:code [ fhir:v "RSON" ] ;
fhir:display [ fhir:v "has reason" ] ;
fhir:definition [ fhir:v "**Description:** The reason or rationale for a service. A reason link is weaker than a trigger, it only suggests that some service may be or might have been a reason for some action, but not that this reason requires/required the action to be taken. Also, as opposed to the trigger, there is no strong timely relation between the reason and the action. As well as providing various types of information about the rationale for a service, the RSON act relationship is routinely used between a SBADM act and an OBS act to describe the indication for use of a medication. Child concepts may be used to describe types of indication.\r\n\r\n*Discussion:* In prior releases, the code \"SUGG\" (suggests) was expressed as \"an inversion of the reason link.\" That code has been retired in favor of the inversion indicator that is an attribute of ActRelationship." ] ;

Source Act must not have the value attribute specified\r\n\r\n**UsageNote:** This relationship allows the result of an observation to be fully expressed as RIM acts as opposed to being embedded in the value attribute. For example, sending a Document act as the result of an imaging observation, sending a list of Procedures and/or other acts as the result of a medical history observation.\r\n\r\nThe valueNegationInd attribute on the source Act has the same semantics of \"negated finding\" when it applies to the target of a VALUE ActRelationship as it does to the value attribute. On the other hand, if the ActRelationship.negationInd is true for a VALUE ActRelationship, that means the specified observation does not have the indicated value but does not imply a negated finding. Because the semantics are extremely close, it is recommended that Observation.valueNegationInd be used, not ActRelationship.negationInd.\r\n\r\n**OpenIssue:** The implications of negationInd on ActRelationship and the valueNegationind on Observation." ] ;

fhir:code [ fhir:v "SPRTBND" ] ;
fhir:display [ fhir:v "has bounded support" ] ;
fhir:definition [ fhir:v "A specialization of \"has support\" (SPRT), used to relate a secondary observation to a Region of Interest on a multidimensional observation, if the ROI specifies the true boundaries of the secondary observation as opposed to only marking the approximate area. For example, if the start and end of an ST elevation episode is visible in an EKG, this relation would indicate the ROI bounds the \"ST elevation\" observation -- the ROI defines the true beginning and ending of the episode. Conversely, if a ROI simply contains ST elevation, but it does not define the bounds (start and end) of the episode, the more general \"has support\" relation is used. Likewise, if a ROI on an image defines the true bounds of a \"1st degree burn\", the relation \"has bounded support\" is used; but if the ROI only points to the approximate area of the burn, the general \"has support\" relation is used." ] ;
